Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Atharvan.тАФс╣гaс╣гс╣нi. yamadevatyam mantroktabakudevatyaс╣Б ca (4, 34. ─Бgneyy─Бu; 5. j─Бtavedas─л; 29. pitry─Б). tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 1-3, 6, 14-18, 20, 22, 23, 25, 30, 34, 36, 46, 48, 50-52, 56. anuс╣гс╣нubh; [4,] 7, 9, 13. jagat─л; 5, 26, 49, 57. bhurij; 19. 3-p. ─Бrс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л; 24. 3-p. samaviс╣гam─Б тАЭrс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л; 37. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 38-44. ─Бrс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л (40, 42-44. bhurij); 45. kakummaty anuс╣гс╣нubh.]

Whitney

Comment

тМКOf the eight “measuring-verses,” 38-45, the first (vs. 38) is a true g─Бyatr─л; the next six (39-44) are mere repetitions of vs. 38, with an ┼лha in the first p─Бda which sometimes spoils the meter; and the last (vs. 45) agrees in its last two p─Бdas with the rest, but has a prior half which is true prose.тМЛ

тМКOf this hymn, only vs. 13 a, b and vs. 17 are found in P─Бipp., in books xix. and xx. respectively. The ritual uses by V─Бit. are naturally very meagre: namely, we find vss. 19-20 used once, and that in the puruс╣гamedha. On the contrary, all but about 18 of the 60 vss. are cited by K─Бu┼Ы. (see under the verses). Bloomfield’s Index may be corrected on page 410 by the insertion of vss. 1-3 (see under vs. 1). Verses 1-3 and 49 constitute, with verses from hymns 1 and 3, parts of an important ritual sequence of 11 verses, as noted under 1. 49. And verses 4-18, the anuс╣гс╣нh─Бn─лs, constitute (with the exception of vs. 10) another such sequence.тМЛ

тМКThe provenience of the material of this hymn.тАФWhereas nearly all of the preceding hymn (all but 4 or 5 out of 61 verses) is found also in the RV., of this hymn, on the other hand, but little more than a third part (hardly 25 vss. out of 60) is RV. material. As elsewhere noted, the hymn begins with 3 vss. which form part of a ritual sequence (of 11 vss.) continuous with the last verses of the preceding hymn.

Griffith

A funeral hymn, taken mainly from the Rigveda

режрез рдпрдорд╛рдп рд╕реЛрдордГрдкрд╡рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. For Yama the soma purifies itself; for Yama is made the oblation; to
    Yama goes the sacrifice, messengered by Agni, made satisfactory.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. x. 14. 13, which, however, in a reads
s├│maс╣Б sunuta, and in b juhut─Б (for kriyate). TA. (vi. 5. 1)
agrees with RV. in both points, but has gachatu in c. The comm.
reads at the end alaс╣Бkс╣Ыtas.

тМКVerses 1, 2, and 3 of this hymn are used (K─Бu┼Ы. 81. 36) in one
continuous sequence with the last four of the preceding hymn (iti
saс╣Бhit─Бс╕е sapta!), to accompany the oblations to Yama in the cremation
ceremony: for details, see my note to xviii. 1. 49.тМЛ

Griffith

For Yama Soma juice flows clear, to Yama is oblation paid. To Yama sacrifice prepared, and heralded by Agni, goes.

режреи рдпрдорд╛рдпрдордзреБрдорддреНрддрдордВ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Offer ye to Yama what is most honeyed, and stand forth; this homage
    to the former-born, the former, the path-making seers.
Notes

This verse and the next correspond to RV. x. 14. 15 and 14, save that
RV. makes our 2 b and 3 b change places* and they become
respectively its 14 b and 15 b, the double inversion thus
leaving our 2 b and 3 b in the same relative position in both
texts. TA. (in vi. 5. l) agrees throughout with RV., both in this verse
and the next. Our 2 b agrees also with RV. i. 15. 9 b. But RV.
in both places has, like TA., juh├│ta for our juh├│t─Б.

*тМКThe case is interesting as showing how easily the component elements
of many of these verses may be shuffled about without detriment to what
we may, out of politeness to the Rishis, call the “sequence of thought.”
The result of the transpositions is best shown by parallel columns,
thus:

[TABLE]

Roth has beautifully illustrated the matter by shuffling together verses
from Schiller’s Riddles (“Von Perlen baut sich eine Br├╝cke” and “Es
steht ein gross’ ger├дumig Haus”): see ZDMG. xxxvii. 109.тАФCf. notes to
xviii. 2. 35; 3. 47.тМЛ

Griffith

Offer to Yama sacrifice most sweet in savour and draw near. Bow down before the Rishis of the olden time, the ancient ones who made the path.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unto Yama the king offer ye an oblation, milk rich in ghee; he
    furnishes (─Б-yam) to us among the living a long life-time, for living
    on.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Do not, O Agni, burn him up; do not be hot upon (abhi-┼Ыuc) him; do
    not warp (kс╣гip) his skin, nor his body; when thou shalt make him done,
    O J─Бtavedas, then send him forward unto the Fathers.
Notes

This verse and the next are RV. x. 16. 1 and 2, but RV. makes our 4
c and 5 a change places (cf. note to our vs. 2). RV., however,
reads ┼Ыocas for ┼Ы┼л┼Ыucas in a, and at the end pitс╣Ы╠Бbhyas тМКas in
our 5 bтМЛ for pitс╣Э╠Бс╣Еr ├║pa. In d, SPP. reads, with RV., ├бthe тАЭm
enam, alleging for his reading three out of eight authorities, as
against two or three that have im├бm. The comm. appears to read ─лm.
Of our mss., all save O.Op.R. give ├бthe тАЩm├бm enam (and O. is corrected
once to this, but the correction struck out again), as our edition
reads; this is so bad a corruption that the authority for the other
should be regarded as sufficient. TA. (in vi. 1. 4) agrees with RV.
except in having kar├бvas in its c тМКour 5 aтМЛ. The text of the
comm. agrees with RV. and TA. in having pitс╣Ыbhyas for pitс╣Эс╣Еr upa,
while the comm. quotes pitс╣Ыbhyas and then adds and explains upa
тМКconstructively a blend-readingтМЛ. Our Bp. appears to give in a
┼Ыu┼Ыucaс╕е, as it тМКapparentlyтМЛ ought to do according to Pr─Бt. iv. 86,
though the example is not quoted in the comment on that rule; but the
other pada-mss. тМКand SPP.тМЛ have ┼Ы┼л┼Ыucaс╕е. The Anukr. is questionable
in its reading as to the verse, whether tristubh or jagatt: the RV.
version is pure tristubh; the AV. one is mixed (12 + 11: 11 + 12). K─Бu┼Ы.
(81. 33) prescribes this verse to be used, with 2. 36; 3. 71, and ii.
34. 5, when the youngest son lights the funeral pile, some of the schol.
declaring vss. 4-7 to be intended instead тМКcf. the comm., page 86┬▓тБ░тМЛ;
then, in 81. 44, vss. 4-9 and 11-18 are called anuс╣гс╣нh─Бn─лs, and are to
be repeated by the anuс╣гс╣нh─Бtс╣Ы during the cremation. тМКRoot kс╣гip
properly means ‘warp’ in its obsolete sense ‘cast or throw.’ If, as I
think, W. is right in rendering the causative here by ‘warp’ = ’twist
out of shape, contort,’ the cases present an interesting semantic
parallel. BR. render by ‘platzen machen.’ Different is the sense of
ava-kс╣гip at 4. 12: see my note.тМЛ

Griffith

Burn him not up, nor quite consume him, Agni. Let not his body or his skin be scattered. O Jatavedas, when thou hast matured him, then send him on his way unto the Fathers.

Translation
  1. When thou shalt make him done, O J─Бtavedas, then commit him to the
    Fathers; when he shall go to that other life (├бsun─лti), then shall he
    become a controller (? va┼Ыan─л╠Б) of the gods.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 16. 2, but RV. makes our 5 a and 4 c change
places: see note to vs. 4. RV. has yad─Б╠Б тМКfor our yad├│ = yad─Б╠Б uтМЛ at
beginning of c, and ├бth─Б at beginning of d. TA. (in vi. 1. 4)
agrees throughout with RV. save in accenting kar├бsi in a. Both, of
course, read ├бthe тАЭm enam in b; but this time the AV. mss. are as
good as unanimous in the corruption of ─лm to im├бm, and both the
published texts are compelled to read it; the Anukr., too, seems to
ratify it, by calling the verse bhurij; the comm. has instead idam,
and one or two of SPP’s authorities follow it. The comm. explains
asun─лti by as┼лn pr─Бс╣З─Бn nayati lok─Бntaram, and hence pr─Бс╣З─Бpahartr─л
devat─Б; and dev─Бn─Бm by svak─лy─Бn─Бm indriy─Бс╣З─Бm; while va┼Ыan─лs is
(cakс╣гur─Бd─лndriy─Бс╣З─Бс╣Б) s┼лry─Бdidevat─Бpr─Бpakaс╕е! тМКWeber deems the idea of
getting the gods under your control to be an indication of lateness or
possibly of Buddhistic influence: Sb. 1895, p. 845, and 1897, p. 597.тМЛ

Griffith

When thou hast made him ready, Jatavedas, then do thou give him over to the Fathers. When he attains unto the life that waits him he will obey the Deities’ commandment.

Translation
  1. With the trikadrukas it purifies itself; six wide ones, verily one
    great one; triс╣гс╣н├║bh, g─Бyatr─л╠Б, the meters: all those [are] set in
    Yama.
Notes

RV. x. 14. 16, the corresponding verse, has in a patati, and at
the end ─Б╠Бhit─Б; TA, (in vi. 5. 3) agrees with it, but transposes
triс╣гс╣н├║bh and g─Бyatr─л╠Б in c. The sense of the verse is wholly
obscure. According to our comm., the trikadrukas are the jyotiс╣гс╣нoma,
goс╣гс╣нoma, and ─Бyuс╣гс╣нoma; the “six wide ones” (f.) are heaven and earth
and day and night and waters and herbs; “the great one” (n.) is taken
тМКalternativelyтМЛ as applying to Yama (m.): mah─Бnt─Бс╣Б yamam uddi┼Ыy─Бi тАЩva
pravartante! The commentator’s ignorance is as great as our own; only
he has no mind to acknowledge it. тМКHillebrandt cites passages akin with

Griffith

With the three jars Brihat alone makes pure the six wide-spread- ing realms. The Gayatri, the Trishtup, all metres in Yama are contained.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go thou to the sun with thine eye, to the wind with thy soul
    (─Бtm├бn); go both to heaven and to earth with [their] due shares (?
    dh├бrman); or go to the waters, if there it is acceptable (hit├б) to
    thee; in the herbs stand firm with thy bodies.

Griffith

The Sun receive thine eye, the wind thy spirit; go, as thy merit is, to earth or heaven. Go, if it be thy lot, unto the waters: go, make thy home in plants with all thy members.

Translation
  1. The goat is the share of the heat (t├бpas); heat thou that; that let
    thine ardor (┼Ыoc├нs) heat, that thy flame (arc├нs); what propitious
    bodies (tan┼л╠Б) are thine, O J─Бtavedas, with them carry him to the world
    of the well-doing.
Notes

The RV. version of this verse has (x. 16. 4) t├бpas─Б in a; in this
case, as seldom, the AV. reading is better. TA. (in vi. 1 . 4) also
gives t├бpas─Б, and it ends differently: vahe тАЩm├бс╣Б sukс╣Ы╠Бt─Бс╣Б y├бtra
lok─Б╠Бс╕е; тМКand it reads aj├│ тАЩbh─Бg├бs, which is explained by its comm. as
bh─Бgarahitaс╕етМЛ. The comm. also has tapas─Б. K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 29) directs the
verse, with 2. 22 (some mss. say, with 2. 57), to be repeated while
“binding a goat on the south,” the anustaraс╣З─л (as which, nevertheless,
the goat is here meant) having been already laid, as a cow, on the body
to be burned. тМКBut see Weber’s treatment of the vs., Sb. 1895, p.
847.тМЛ

Griffith

Thy portion is the goat: with heat consume him: let thy fierce flame, thy glowing splendour, burn him. With thine auspicious forms, O Jatavedas, bear this man to the region of the pious.

Griffith

Let all thy rapid flames, O Jatavedas, wherewith thou fillest heaven and earth’s mid-region, Follow the goat as he goes on, united: then with the others, most auspicious, aid us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Release again, O Agni, to the Fathers him who goes (car) offered
    to thee, with svadh─Б╠Б; clothing himself in life (─Б╠Бyus), let him go
    unto [his] posterity (? ┼Ы├йс╣гas); let him be united with a body, very
    splendid.
Notes

The corresponding verse in RV. (x. 16. 5) reads at end of b
svadh─Б╠Бbhis, in c vetu for y─Бtu, and at end j─Бtavedaс╕е (for
suv├бrc─Бс╕е); TA. (in vi. 4. 2) also has svadh─Б╠Бbhis and j─Бtavedas,
but in c gives ├║pa y─Бtu ┼Ы├йс╣гam. тМКThe last p─Бda, d, recurs below
at 3. 58.тМЛ The third p─Бda is of doubtful meaning, but perhaps relates to
the return of the deceased, after due installation among the Manes, to
receive the ancestral offerings. The comm. explains ┼Ы├йс╣гas тМКwhich he
takes as ┼Ыeс╣гa-s, masc.тМЛ simply as apatyan─Бman. тМКK─Бu┼Ы. 81. 44 excepts
this verse from the sequence of 14 anuс╣гс╣нh─Бn─л versts (4-18): see under
vs. 4.тМЛ In K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 28) the verse is used in the ceremonies of the
third day after cremation, in connection with sprinkling and collecting
the bones. The Anukr. takes no notice of the deficiency of a syllable in
d. тМКAs to ┼Ыeс╣гas, see my note on this vs., Reader, p. 379-380:
W’s interpretation seems to me much better than either of those there
noted.тМЛ

Griffith

Away O Agni, to the Fathers, send him who, offered in thee, goes with our oblations. Wearing new life let him approach his offspring, and splendid, be invested with a body,

Whitney
Translation
  1. Run thou past the two four-eyed, brindled dogs of Saram─Б, by a happy
    (s─Бdh├║) road; then go unto the beneficent Fathers, who revel in common
    revelry with Yama.
Notes

The corresponding verse in RV. is x. 14. 10. RV. puts s─Бramey─Б├║ before
┼Ыv─Б╠Бn─Бu: тМКand with this order (but not with that of AV.), the
resolution to ┼Ыu─Б╠Бn─Бu is effective in giving a normal rhythmтМЛ. RV.
reads in c ├бth─Б for ├бdh─Б, and ├║pa for ├бpi; TA. (in vi. 3. 1)
has ├бp─л тАЩhi, but agrees otherwise with RV. The comm. gives instead
ape тАЩhi; and it explains this difficult reading by either taking apa
as used in the sense of upa, or else understanding it to mean “go away
[from the dogs]”! The Anukr. pays no attention to the redundant
syllable in b, тМКunless it assumes a deficiency in a to balance
itтМЛ. The verse (according to the comm., vss. 11-13) is used (K─Бu┼Ы. 81.
22) when the two kidneys of the accompanying sacrificed animal are (by
way of a “sop to Cerberus”) put into the hands of the dead man on the
funeral pile. Then verses 11-18 are (K─Бu┼Ы. 80. 35) mentioned and used
with the hariс╣З─лs (see under 1. 61); and by the schol. тМКsee note to
K─Бu┼Ы. 82. 31тМЛ and the comm. they are reckoned themselves as hariс╣З─лs.
The comm. further prescribes them as accompanying the transfer of the
dead body to the place of cremation.

Griffith

Run and outspeed the two dogs, Sarama’s offspring, brindled, four-eyed, upon thy happy pathway. Draw nigh thou to the gracious-minded Fathers who take their pleasure in the feast with Yama.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What two defending dogs thou hast, O Yama, four-eyed, sitting by the
    road, men-watching, with them, O king, do thou surround him; assign to
    him well-being and freedom from disease.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 14. 11, which in b reads pathir├бkс╣г─л
nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гas─Бu, and for c t─Бbhy─Бm enam p├бri dehi r─Бjan (our dhehi
is a corruption), and in d inserts ca after svast├н. TA. (in vi.
3. 1) agrees with RV. except in having -c├бkс╣гas─Б, and in placing
r─Бjan and enam in c as does AV. The comm. makes a compound of
yamarakс╣гit─Бr─Бu in a; and it declares pari dhehi in c to =
paridehi.

Griffith

And those two dogs of thine, Yama, the watchers, four-eyed who look on men and guard the pathway Entrust this man, O King, to their protection, and with prosperity and health endow him.

  1. Broad-nosed, feeding on lives (? asutс╣Ы╠Бp), copper-colored, Yama’s

Griffith

Dark-hued, insatiate, with distended nostrils, Yama’s two envoys roam among the people. May they restore to us a fair existence here and to-day that we may see the sunlight.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Soma purifies itself for some; some wait upon (upa-─Бs) ghee; for
    whom honey runs forward (?), unto them do thou go.
Notes

The ‘go’ in these verses is gachat─Бt, imperative of remoter or after
action. The translation implies restoration in c of the RV. (x. 154.

  1. reading pradh─Б╠Бvati, of which our pradh─Б╠Бv (p. praре░dh─Б├║) ├бdhi
    seems only a blundering and unintelligible corruption. Some of our mss.
    (and one of SPP’s) accent pradh─Б╠Бvadhi. The comm. agrees with RV., and
    SPP. is not to be blamed for adopting, though against all the
    authorities save the comm., pradh─Б╠Бvati in his text. TA. (which has our
    vss. 14, 17, and 16 following immediately after our 11-13, little as the
    two sets appear to have to do with each other) reads (in vi. 3. 2) with
    RV.

тМКSee p. xcii.тМЛ

Griffith

For some the Soma juice runs clear some sit by sacrificial oil. To those for whom the meath flows forth, even to those let him depart.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They who of old were won by right, born of right, increasers of
    rightтАФto the seers rich in fervor (t├бpas-), born of fervor, O Yama, do
    thou go.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 154. 4) reads in a, b p┼л╠Бrva с╣Ыtas─Б╠Бpa
с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Бnaс╕е in c pitс╣Э╠Бn, in d t─Б╠Бс╣Е┼Ы cid ev├б (as in our vss. 14,
16, 17). The comm. explains yama here to mean yamavan niyata, or
yamena n─лyam─Бna preta, which is probably not far from correct; it is
the deceased person who is addressed.

Griffith

Let him, O Yama, go to those Rishis austere, of Fervour born, First followers of Law, the sons of Law, upholders of the Law.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They who by fervor are unassailable, who by fervor have gone to
    heaven (sv├аr), who made fervor their greatness, unto them do thou go.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 154. 2) has no variant; in TA. (vi. 3.
2), however, we find gat─Б╠Бs for yay├║s in b, and mah├бt for
m├бhas in c: this latter reading the comm. appears to have in mind
when he explains mahas as signifying mahat.

Translation
  1. They who fight in the contests (pradh├бna), who are
    self-sacrificing (tan┼лty├бj) heroes, or who give thousand-fold
    sacrificial gifts, unto them do thou go.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 154. 3) has no variant; TA. (in vi. 3.

c, t─Бs tvaс╣Б sahasradakс╣гiс╣З─Бс╕е, and in d gachat─Бm.

Griffith

The heroes who contend in war and boldly cast their lives away. Or who give guerdon thousandfold,–even to those let him depart.

Let him, O Yama, go to those Rishis austere, of Fervour born, Skilled in a thousand ways and means, the sages who protect the Sun.

In the free amplitude of earth take roomy space to lodge thee in. Let all oblations which in life thou paidest drop thee honey now.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I call thy mind hither with mind; come unto these houses, enjoying
    [them]; unite thyself with the Fathers, with Yama; let pleasant,
    helpful (? ┼Ыagm├б) winds blow thee unto [them].
Notes

Excepting K., all our mss. read im─Б╠Бm (or im─Б╠Бс╣Б) in b; SPP.
records the reading as given only by two of his pada-mss. тМКP─Бda c
is RV. x. 14. 8 a.тМЛ The comm. glosses ┼Ыagm─Бs with sukhakar─Бs.
The Anukr. does not heed the redundant syllable in b.

Griffith

Hither I call thy spirit with my spirit. Come thou; delighted, to these dwelling-places. Unite thee with the Fathers and with Yama: strong and delicious be the winds that fan thee.

рд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛реСрдорд┐ред рддреЗреТред рдордиреСрд╕рд╛ред рдордирдГреСред рдЗреТрд╣ред рдЗреТрдорд╛рдиреНред рдЧреГреТрд╣рд╛рдиреНред рдЙрдкреСред рдЬреБреТрдЬреБреТрд╖рд╛реТрдгрдГред рдЖред рдЗреТрд╣рд┐реТред рд╕рдореНред рдЧреТрдЪреНрдЫреТрд╕реНрд╡реТред рдкрд┐реТрддреГрд╜рднрд┐рдГреСред рд╕рдореНред рдпреТрдореЗрдиреСред рд╕реНрдпреЛреТрдирд╛рдГред рддреНрд╡рд╛реТред рд╡рд╛рддрд╛рдГреСред рдЙрдкреСред рд╡рд╛реТрдиреНрддреБреТред рд╢реТрдЧреНрдорд╛рдГред реи.реирезред

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Griffith

I have recalled thy life to life, to being, power, and energy. Let thy soul go unto its own: so to the Fathers hasten thou.

Translation
  1. Let nothing whatever of thy mind, nor of thy life (├бsu), nor of
    thy members, nor of thy sap, nor of thy body, be left here.
Notes

The translation implies emendation of m├бnas to m├бnasas, as called
for by the connection and by the meter. The Anukr. scans the verse as 6

  • 8: 10 = 24. Bs.E. have tanv─Б╠Ас╕е in c. This verse, with 26 below,
    is used by K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 29) in connection with gathering up the bones
    after cremation; with the same, and further with 3. 25-37, in connection
    (85. 26) with their interment. тМКFor its general purport, see Weber,
    Sb. 1894, p. 775, note 2.тМЛ
Griffith

Let not thy soul be left behind: here let not aught of thee remain, Of spirit, body, members, sap.

Let not a tree oppness thee, nor Earth the great Goddess weigh thee down. Among the Fathers find thy home, and thrive mid those whom Yama rules.

    [or] breath has gone forth upon the wind (?), let the associated
    (s├бn─лс╕Нa) Fathers, assembling, make that enter thee again, bit
    (gh─Бs├б) from bit.

Griffith

Each parted member, severed from thy body, thy vital breaths that in the wind have vanished, With all of these, piece after piece, shall Fathers who dwell to- gether meet and reunite thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The living have excluded this man from their houses; carry ye him
    out, forth from this village; death was the kindly messenger of Yama; he
    made his life-breaths (├бsu) go to the Fathers.
Notes

The verse is used in K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 18) with an oblation to the fires, when
preparing the body of the deceased for cremation. тМКNote that the
“messengers” or “men” of death or of Yama play a r├┤le in the Buddhist
literature: see An╠Дguttara Nik─Бya, iii. 4 (35: p. 138), Devad┼лta Vagga;
J─Бtaka, i., p. 138┬▓тБ┤, and scholion; Journal of the P─Бli Text Society,
1885, p. 62.тМЛ

Griffith

Him have the living banished from their houses: remove him to a distance from the hamlet. Yama’s observant messenger was Mrityu he hath despatched men’s lives unto the Fathers.

about and then flung away.

Griffith

Those Dasyus who, not eating our oblations, come wilh friends’ faces mingled with the Fathers, Those who wear gross those who wear subtile bodies,–from this. our sacrifice let Agni blast them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let there enter together (sam-vi┼Ы) here our own Fathers, doing
    what is pleasant, lengthening [our] life-time; may we be able to reach
    them with oblation, living long for numerous autumns.
Notes

The translation implies in a the pada-reading sv─Б╠Бс╕е: naс╕е, which
SPP. gives by emendation, all the pada-mss. save Bp. (which has sv─Б╠Б:
naс╕е) having sv─Б╠Бnaс╕е; again, it implies in b praре░tir├бntaс╕е, while
all read praре░tir├бnte тМКor -ateтМЛ; here also SPP. emends to -ntaс╕е.
The comm. reads -nte, and glosses it by pravardhayantu! тМКA similar
uncertainty (as between the Vulgate and Ppp.) concerning the
understanding of the combination pratiranta ─Бyuс╕е was noted by me under
xiv. 2. 36.тМЛ The verse is used, according to K─Бu┼Ы. (83. 29), next after
the use of 1. 52, in arranging the bones for burial; and it is repeated,
like the latter, in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a (87. 28); sam-vi┼Ы, as here
applied, perhaps has its secondary sense of ’turn in, lie down.’ The
comm. reads dakс╣гam─Бс╣З─Бs in c, explaining it by vardham─Бn─Бs. The
Anukr. does not notice the redundant syllable in c тМКor perhaps
assumes a deficiency in d to balance it. The word nakс╣г- demands an
accusative: so that both meter and syntax combine to cast suspicion on
tebhyasтМЛ.

Griffith

Bringing delight, prolonging our existence, here let our own, the Fathers, dwell together. Coming with sacrifice may we assist them, living long lives through many autumn seasons.

Translation
  1. What milch-cow I set down (ni-pс╣Ы) for thee, and what rice-dish for
    thee in milk (kс╣г─лr├б)тАФwith that mayest thou be the supporter of the
    person (j├бna) who is there (├бtra) without a living.
Notes

That is, ‘without the means of sustaining life.’ Our Bp.E. read
aj─лvanas, unaccented; the normal accent would be aj─лvan├бs. The comm.
remarks that ni-pс╣Ы is used distinctively of a gift for the Fathers
(pitrye d─Бne vartate).

Griffith

Now by this cow I bring thee, by the boiled rice set in milk for thee, Be the supporter of the folk left here without a livelihood.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Pass forward [over a stream] rich in horses, which is very
    propitious, or, further on, an с╣Ыkс╣г─Б╠Бka, more new; he who slew thee, be
    he one to be killed; let him not find any other portion.
Notes

The first half-verse is extremely obscure, and its translation only
mechanical; we may conjecture that its text is corrupt. Such a
combination as -v─Б: с╣Ыkс╣г- (so all the pada-texts read) into -v─Б
rkс╣г- is contrary to grammatical rule, unauthorized by the Pr─Бt., and
unsupported, so far as I know, by any second case. Part of our
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. (P.M.E.I.) have -v─Б с╣Ыkс╣г-, but that is equally abnormal;
SPP. makes no mention of any such reading among his authorities.
“Stream” is supplied to a┼Ыv─Бvat─лm because K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 10) prescribes
the verse to be used, in the ceremonies of the first day after
cremation, on crossing a stream, and pr├б tara naturally suggests it.
─А┼Ыv─Бvat─лm is unquestionably the AV. text; it is quoted as an example
of long ─Б in such a position under Pr─Бt. iii. 17. One may conjecture
as a plausible emendation ├б┼Ыmanvat─лm pr├б taray─Б su┼Ы├йv─Бm (cf. for
├б┼Ыmanvat─л xii. 2. 26, 27; and our comm. reads here taraya for tara
y─Б╠Б). Then с╣Ыkс╣г─Б╠Бka might possibly be a region or road тМКbeyond the
riverтМЛ ‘infested by bears’ (с╣Ы╠Бkс╣гa: so the comm.); the word с╣Ыkс╣г─Б╠Бka is
ignored by both Pet. Lexx. тМКsave in so far as this vs. is cited by the
Major Lex. under с╣Ыkс╣г─л╠Бk─БтМЛ. тМКWeber takes it as ’the milky way’:
Festgruss an Roth, p. 138.тМЛ But it is of little use to speculate in
such a case. SPP. reads in c vadhyas, with (as he reports) all his
authorities save two; we also have both va- and ba- among our mss.,
but I cannot specify all that favor the one reading or the other. The
lacking syllable in b, not noticed by the Anukr., helps in its
degree to indicate corruption of text.

Griffith

Prolong the pleasant Dawn enriched with horses-or bearing us. anew beyond the darkness. Adjudged to die be he, the man who slew thee: this portion let him find, and not another.

Griffith

Yama is higher and Vivasvan lower: nothing whatever do I see above him. This sacrifice of mine is based on Yama, Vivasvan spread the atmosphere about us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They hid away the immortal one (f.) from mortals; having made one of
    like color, they gave her to Vivasvant; what that was carried also the
    two A┼Ыvins; and Saraс╣Зy┼л deserted two twins.
Notes

Whether ’two pairs of twins’ is meant is not altogether certain; but
that would be strictly dv├й mithun├й; тМКbut see BR. v. 777, line 3тМЛ. The
verb abharat does not mean ‘bore,’ in the sense of ‘gave birth to,’
though it might mean ‘carried [in her womb],’ and so might have a
nearly equivalent value; our comm. renders it by samabharat or
udap─Бdayat. The third p─Бda means ’that substitute, whatever it really
was,’ though the usual version “when that was” (for y├бt t├бd ─Б╠Бs─лt) is
not altogether impossible. The verse is RV. x. 17. 2, which differs only
by reading in b kс╣Ыtv─л╠Б and adadus (for which our -dhus is a
common corruption). It is properly inseparable from 1. 53 above; тМКfor
bibliographical references, see under that vs.тМЛ. K─Бu┼Ы. and V─Бit. pass it
unused, as they did 1. 53. тМКThe comm., with one or two of SPP’s mss.,
reads amс╣Ыt─Бn in a.тМЛ

Griffith

From mortal men they hid the immortal Lady, made one like her and gave her to Vivasvan. Saranyu brought to him the Asvin brothers, and then deserted both twinned pairs of children.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They that are buried, and they that are scattered (vap) away, they
    that are burned and they that are set up (├║ddhita)тАФall those Fathers,
    O Agni, bring thou to eat the oblation.
Notes

─Аp. (in i. 8. 7) has a verse analogous with this; the divisions there
are тМКye garbhe mamrus,тМЛ par─Бst─Бs, uddhat─Бs, and nikh─Бt─Бs. The
comm. explains paropt─Бs by d┼лrade┼Ыe k─Бс╣гс╣нhavat parityakt─Бс╕е; but
uddhit─Бs by saс╣Бsk─Бrottarak─Бlam ┼лrdhamde┼Ыe pitс╣Ыloke sthit─Бс╕е! it
evidently refers to exposure on something elevated, such as is practised
by many peoples. The pada-text reads ├║ddhit─Бс╕е, undivided, by Pr─Бt.
iv. 63. The verse (according to K─Бu┼Ы. 87. 22) is used, with 3. 47, 48
and 4. 41, in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a ceremony, to accompany the setting up
of one of two lighted sticks (cf. under 1. 56) and piling fuel around
it.

Griffith

Bring thou the Fathers one and all Agni, to eat the sacrifice. The buried, and the cast away, those burnt with fire, and those exposed.

Translation
  1. They who, burned with fire, [and] who, not burned with fire, revel
    on svadh─Б╠Б in the midst of heavenтАФthem thou knowest, if thine, O
    J─Бtavedas; let them enjoy with svadh─Б╠Б the sacrifice, the sv├бdhiti.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. x. 15. 14 a, b and 13 c, d (and to
VS. xix. 60 a, b and 67 c, d). In the first half, AV. and RV.
agree (two of our mss., O.R., combine y├й тАШnag-); VS. has -с╣гv─Бtt─Бs
both times for -dagdh─Бs. For c, RV. and VS. read tv├бс╣Б vettha y├бti
t├й j─Бt- ’thou knowest how many they are,’ and of this our text is
doubtless a corruption. Nearly half the mss. have te (both editions,
with the remaining mss., including our O.R.T.K., t├й); the translation
implies te. HGS. (ii. 11. 1) has agne t─Бn vettha yadi te j─Бtavedaс╕е.
For d, RV. and VS. have svadh─Б╠Бbhir yaj├▒├бс╣Б s├║kс╣Ыtaс╣Б juс╣гasva; and
here again our text seems only a corruption; sv├бdhitim (p.
sv├бре░dhitim) must be meant as nomen actionis to svadh─Б╠Б, I think, =
’the giving of svadh─Б╠Б’тАФa false formation. The comm. reads svadh─Бy─Бs
and svadhitam, explaining the latter as svadh─Б saс╣Бj─Бt─Б yasya.
According to the comm., this verse and the preceding are used in the
piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a “on laying two pieces of fuel.”

Griffith

Those, whether flames have burnt or not consumed them, who in the midst of heaven enjoy oblations– Let them, when thou dost know them, Jatavedas, accept with sacred food the axe and worship.

Translation
  1. Burn (tap) thou propitiously (┼Ы├бm); do not burn overmuch; O
    Agni, do not burn the body; be thy vehemence (┼Ы├║с╣гma) in the woods; on
    the earth be what is thy violence (h├бras).
Notes

Two of our mss. (R.s.m.Op.), and one of SPP’s reciters, leave tapas at
end of b unaccented; and this is, of course, more correct. For the
application of the verse according to K─Бu┼Ы., see under 2. 4, with which
it is closely akin in sense. тМКThe comm. reads tanvas in b.тМЛ

Griffith

Burn gently, Agni, burn not up the body with too fervent heat. Let all thy force and fury be expended on the woods and earth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I give this release to him who hath thus come and hath become mine
    hereтАФthus replies the knowing YamaтАФlet this one approach (upa-sth─Б) my
    wealth here.
Notes

The translation implies that r─Бy├б before ├║pa in d means r─Бy├бs
(accus. pl.), and not r─Бy├й as understood by the pada-text; the comm.
understands r─Бyas. Also, that c├йd in b admits of being taken as
ca ├нd тМКthe pada-text always reads ca: ├нt, even when the meaning is
‘if’тМЛ with individual meaning, and not as the compound particle, = ‘if.’
тМКThere is a gap in the commentary just after the explanation of etat:
but the commentator’s text of the AV.тМЛ reads y├бt for y├бs at
beginning of b. For the K─Бu┼Ы. use of the verse with 1. 55, see under
the latter. This verse also accompanies (with 3. 73: K─Бu┼Ы. 85. 24) the
deposition of the bones in the hole in the ceremony of interment.

Griffith

I give this place to him who hath come hither and now is mine, to be a home to rest in: This was the thought of Yama when he answered: This man is. mine. Let him come here to riches.

Translation
  1. They that departed unmarried [but] assiduous, abandoning hatreds,
    having no progenyтАФthey, going up to heaven (div), have found a place
    (lok├б), тМКthey,тМЛ shining (? d─л╠Бdhy─Бna) upon the back of the firmament.

religious duties) by ┼Ыaс╣Еsam─Бna or else (from root ┼Ыa┼Ы ’leap’)

in d as meant for d─лdy─Бna; the comm. renders by d─лpyam─Бna. The

Griffith

Unmarried men who toiled and have departed, the childless, having left their foes behind them, Have found on high the world whereto they mounted, reflecting on the ridge of vaulted heaven.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Watery is the lowest heaven (d├нv), full of stars (? p─лlu-) is
    called the midmost; the third is called the fore-heaven (prad├нv), in
    which the Fathers sit.
Notes

Rather than leave p─лlu- in b untranslated, we set in our version
the comm’s worthless etymological guess (p─Бlayant─л тАЩti p─лlavaс╕е:
grahanakс╣гatr─Бdayaс╕е). SPP. has at the beginning the better accent
udanv├бt─л, as read by half his autliorities (and by our O.Op.R. among
those collated after publication). Our Bp.D. accent also p─лlumat─л╠Б; O.
reads p─лt├║mat─л, doubtless an accidental blunder, yet suggesting the
emendation pitum├бt─л ‘rich in nourishment.’ For the use of the verse
prescribed by K─Бu┼Ы., see under 1. 61; the comm. says simply that with
this verse and another one (iti dv─Бbhy─Бm) the body is raised in order
to being laid on the cart or litter (for transportation to the funeral
pile); a schol. (note to K─Бu┼Ы. 82. 31) uses it also in connection with
the interment of the bone-relics.

Griffith

The lowest is the Watery heaven, Pilumati the middlemost; The third and highest, that wherein the Fathers dwell, is called Pradyaus.

рекреп рдпреЗ рди ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. They that are our father’s fathers, that are [his] grandfathers,
    that entered the wide atmosphere, they that dwell upon earth and heaven
    (d├нv)тАФto those Fathers would we pay worship with homage.
Notes

The first half-verse is found again below as 3. 59 a, b. The verse
is used (K─Бu┼Ы. 81. 37) тМКas the last one of eleven verses (see my note to
xviii. 1. 49) which accompany the oblations offered to Yama and poured
upon the corpse (comm., vol. iv., p. 115┬╣тБ╖: he says iti dv─Бbhy─Бm) in
the cremation ceremony after the fire is lightedтМЛ.

Griffith

The Fathers of our Father, his Grandfathers, those who have entered into air’s wide region, Those who inhabit earth or dwell in heaven, these Fathers will we worship with oblation.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This time, verily, not further (├бparam), seest thou the sun in the
    heaven (d├нv); as a mother her son with her hem (s├нc), do thou cover
    him, O earth.
Notes

The last half-verse is RV. x. 18. 11 c, d, without variant (TA., in
vi. 7. 1, has at the end bh┼лmi vс╣Ыс╣Зu), and is also found below as 3. 50
c, d. K─Бu┼Ы. (86. 10) applies the verse, with 3.49 and 4. 66, in
raising a pile over the interred bones; according to the comm. тМКvol.
iv., p. 115тМЛ, the pile is of an uneven number of sticks (┼Ыal─Бk─Б) or
bricks, and vss. 50-52 are to be used. тМКOver “hem” W. interlines
“skirt.” “Border of the garment” says our comm., cel─Б├▒calena.тМЛ тМКAs to
this beautiful verse, see Weber, Sb. 1895, p. 861, and cf. the
epilogue to the I┼Ы─Б Upanishad, especially vss. 15, 16.тМЛ

Griffith

Thou seest now, and ne’er again shalt look upon, the Sun in heaven. Cover him as a mother draws her skirt about her son, O Earth!

релрез рдЗрджрдорд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЙрдирд╛рдкрд░рдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This time, verily; not further; in old age another further than
    this; as a wife her husband with her garment, do thou cover him, O earth
    (bh┼л╠Бmi).
Notes

The first half-verse is very obscure, and the second p─Бda perhaps
corrupt. The comm. takes jar├бsi with the first p─Бda, and explains that
“what food etc. has been enjoyed in old age, this verily, left over, not
anything else [further], is to be enjoyed”; and then “than this place
of interment, any other place is not found for him”; all of which is
simply silly. The Anukr. pays no attention to the redundant syllable
(unless we pronounce patim тАШva) in c.

Griffith

This once,,and at no other time hereafter in a lengthened life: Cover him, as a wife, O Earth, covers her husband with her robe!

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni-and-Soma, makers of roads, ye have distributed (vi-dh─Б) to
    the gods a pleasant treasure [and] world; send ye unto [us] P┼лshan,
    who shall carry by goat-traveled roads him that goes thither.
Notes

The translation implies emendation at the end of gachatam to
g├бchantam, which seems necessary in order to make sense; the
corruption to the former may have been made because it better suits the
meter.тАФтМКThe translation also implies the reading pr├йс╣гyatam, which is
given in the Berlin text and is supported byтМЛ our Op. (pr├б: iс╣гyatam),
by SPP’s тМКCP. (pr├б: ─лс╣гyatam) and by hisтМЛ Dc. secunda manu: all the
rest read pr├йс╣гyantam (p. pr├б: iс╣г- or pr├б: ─лс╣г-), which SPP.
accordingly adopts in his saс╣Бhit─Б-text; тМКbut in his pada-text he
prints pr├б: ─л╠Бс╣гyantam, and he mentions the accent in his noteтМЛ. The
comm. glosses preс╣гyantam with pragacchantam in his usual loose and
easy way.тАФNearly all our mss. also have ajoy─Б╠Бn─Бis (p. ajaс╕ере░y-) in
d; we followed Bs. in giving ajay- (which the translation
implies). тМКWeber also accepts the reading ajay- and interprets it as
’traveled by man’s unborn (a-ja) or immortal part, i.e. his spirit’:
Festgruss an Roth, p. 138 and note 5.тМЛ On the authority of a single
ms., SPP. accepts as his reading a├▒joy─Б╠Бn─Бis; тМКas to this matter, see
my note marked with a * in the next paragraphтМЛ. The reading
a├▒joy─Б╠Бn─Бis had already been conjectured by the Pet. Lexx.; тМКso BR. v.
959, with the meaning ’leading straight to the goal’: cf. OB. i. 18 bтМЛ.
The reading a├▒jay- is given by two or three of SPP’s mss.; among them
is that of the comm., who explains by a├▒jas─Б, ─Бrjavena y─Бnti…ebhiс╕е.
The “goat-traveled” roads, of course, are those to which P┼лс╣гan’s team of
goats are wonted.тАФTwo of SPP’s authorities give dadhatus in b; the
comm. reads dadhatus in one of two alternative explanations, and
-thus in the other.тАФPossibly v├н before lok├бm is to be taken as
belonging to this word alone: ‘ye have assigned to the gods a pleasant
treasure.’ тМКI do not see what W. means by the last sentence.тМЛтАФFor the
use of the verse by K─Бu┼Ы. etc., see under 1. 61 and 2. 48; the comm.
includes with it vss. 54 and 55. It exceeds a proper triс╣гс╣нubh by two
syllables.

* тМКIn reading a├▒joy─Б╠Бn─Бis, SPP. is supported in fact by three or four
of his mss. (B.C.R.Dc.p.m.) and presumably also by at least three of his
pada-mss., since he reports nothing to the contrary. Moreover, he
thinks that further support is given him by the reading a├▒j─Бy- of two
of his authorities (Dc. sec. manu, and the reciter V.), which reading,
as he says, may represent an ill-corrected reading a├▒joy-; and perhaps
the aj─Бuy- of the reciter K. points in the same direction, to
a├▒joy-. As between the readings a├▒joy- and ajay-, even Whitney’s
mss. point decidedly to a├▒joy-.тАФLeaving the mss. of this passage out
of account, however, the word a├▒joy─Б╠Бna is well supported by its exact
synonym a├▒jas─Б╠Бyana, p. a├▒jas─Бре░├бyana, used four times of the paths
(srut├н) by which one goes to the heavenly world (TS. vii. 2. 1┬▓; 3.
5┬│; 4. 1┬│: also AB. iv. 17, here as the exact opposite of a ‘roundabout
road’ mah┬п├бpathaс╕е pary─Бс╣Зaс╕е), and also by the doubtless precisely
equivalent a├▒jas─л╠Бn─Бm (srut├нm) of the Rigveda (x. 32. 7).тАФThis last
phrase S─Бyaс╣Зa explains alternatively by с╣Ыjum akuс╣нilam m─Бrgam; cf. his
similar explanation of path├│ devatr─Б╠Б тАЩ├▒jase тАЩva y─Б╠Бn─Бn at x. 73. 7; cf.
also a├▒jas─Бyano, used in the D─лgha Nik─Бya, xiii. 4 ff., as a synonym
of uju-maggo: all of which is in most perfect accord with the
above-mentioned ─Бrjavena etc. of our comm., whose testimony therefore

true reading and ajay- the corrupt one, the corruption is a very

x. 26. 8; and the occurrences of aj─Б╠Б┼Ыva) consists of goats.тМЛ

Griffith

Ye have prepared, pathmakers, Agni-Soma, a fair world for the Gods to be the it treasure. Go to that world and send us Pushan hither to bear us on the paths the goat hath trodden.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let P┼лshan, knowing, urge thee forth from hereтАФhe, the shepherd of
    creation (bh├║vana) who loses no cattle; may he commit thee to those
    Fathers, [and] Agni to the beneficent gods.
Notes

The RV. has a corresponding verse (x. 17. 3), without variant. TA. (in
vi. 1. i) has in c dad─Бt (as has our comm.), and at the end
suvid├бtrebhyas. The mss. are somewhat equally divided in c-d
between -bhyo тАШgn├нr and -bhyo agn├нr; our text adopts the latter;
SPP., better, the former, with RV. and TA.

Griffith

Guard of the world, whose cattle ne’er are injured, may Pushan bear thee hence, for he hath knowledge. May he consign thee to these Fathers’ keeping, and to the gracious Gods let Agni give hee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. May life-time, having all life-time, protect thee about; let P┼лshan
    protect thee in front on the forward road; where sit the well-doers,
    whither they have gone, there let god Savitar set thee.
Notes

RV., in the corresponding verse (x. 17. 4), reads p─Бsati in a, and
t├й yay├║s at end of c тМКthus rectifying the meter in both placesтМЛ;
and TA. (in vi. 1. 2) agrees with it both times; the comm. also has
p─Бsati. The verse is metrically irregular (10 + 11: 12 + 11 = 44);
тМКbut perfectly good in its RV. form (11 + 11: 12 + 11)тМЛ.

Griffith

Lord of all life, let Ayu guard thee, Pushan convey thee forward on the distant pathway. May Savitar the God conduct thee thither where dwell the pious who have gone before thee.

Translation
  1. I yoke for thee these two conveyers тМКv├бhniтМЛ, to convey (vah)

Notes

Ava, in d, is so strange that we can only regard it as a
corruption for ├бpi, which TA. reads in the corresponding verse (in vi.

  1. 1). TA. also has the better reading -n─лth─Бya in b тМКso both
    editionsтМЛ, as has also the comm., though its explanation seems rather to
    imply -n─лt─Бya. TA. further has the bad accent vahn─л╠Б in a, and
    gives in c y─Б╠Бbhy─Бm, and in d (for s├бmit─лs) sukс╣Ы╠Бt─Бm. The
    comm. has sam iti, talking sam as joint prefix with ava, and iti
    as anena prak─Бreс╣Зa; our Bp.E. read s├бmit─л ca; possibly the comm’s
    error is akin with this. According to K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 34), the verse is used
    when two draft-oxen, or two men, are harnessed to draw the body to the
    funeral pile.
Griffith

For thee I yoke these carriers twain to bear thee to the spirit. world. Hasten with them to Yama’s home and join his gathered. companies.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This garment hath now come first to thee; remove (apa-┼лh) that one
    which thou didst wear here before; knowing, do thou follow along with
    what is offered and bestowed, where it is given thee variously among
    them of various connection (? v├нbandhu).
Notes

TK. (in vi. 1. 1) has a corresponding verse, but with sundry variants:
at the beginning, id├бс╣Б (which is better) tv─Б v├бstram; in c, d,
├бnu s├бm pa┼Ыya d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Бс╣Б y├бth─Б te. Te datt├бm is perhaps better ‘given
by thee’тАФthy former deeds of religion and charity, now to be enjoyed in
their fruit; and v├нbandhu ’to those not thine own connections.’ The
Pet. Lexx. explain v├нbandhuс╣гu as ‘destitute of connections or
relatives.’ The comm., with its customary regardlessness of accent,
understands the word as two words, vi bandhuс╣гu, and connects vi (=
vi┼Ыeс╣гeс╣Зa) with dattam. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 80. 17, the verse is used,
with 4. 31, in connection with dressing the body for cremation; in 81.
29, some of the mss. substitute it for vs. 22 above. Some of the schol.
(note to K─Бu┼Ы. 80. 52) use it and 4. 31 when the body is laid on the
funeral pile. The verse, as a triс╣гс╣нubh, is rather svar─Бj than
bhurij (11 + 12: 11 + 12 = 46).

Griffith

This is the robe that first was wrapped about thee: cast off the robe thou worest here among us. Go, knowing, to the meed of virtuous action, thy many gifts. bestowed upon the friendless.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wrap about thee of kine a protection from the fire; cover thyself up
    with grease and fatness, lest the bold one, exulting with violence
    (h├бras), shake thee strongly (dadс╣Ы╠Бс╕е) about, intending to consume
    thee.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse is x. 16. 7; in b it transposes m├йdas─Б
and p─л╠Бvas─Б, and in d it has vidhakс╣гy├бn paryan╠Дkh├бy─Бte, which is
decidedly better. TA. (in vi. 1. 4) reads d├бdhad vidhakс╣гy├бn
paryan╠Дkh├бy─Бt─Бi. Our vidhakс╣г├бn, though read by both editions, is only
another example of the not infrequent careless omission of y after a
с╣г or ┼Ы; only one of our mss. (Op.) reads -kс╣гy├бn, but five of SPP’s
authorities give -kс╣гyan (as against six with -kс╣гan), and it is much
to be wondered at that he has not adopted it in his text; the comm.
seems to read -kс╣гan, but explains as if -kс╣гyan (vi┼Ыeс╣гeс╣Зa dagdhum
icchan). At the end we ought to read parin╠Дkh├бy─Бt─Бi, and SPP. gives
that, with the majority of his mss., the rest having, with our text,
p├бr─лn╠Дkhay-; of our mss., only two of the later collated ones (O.Op.)
have the proper accent; Bp. has p├бriре░─лn╠Дkhay─Бt─Бi, which is absurd*;
the comm. treats pari as an independent word (as if the reading were
p├бr─л тАЭn╠Дkh├бy─Бt─Бi). The comm. glosses dadhс╣Ы╠Бk by pragalbhas; тМКcf. my
Noun-Inflection, JAOS. x. 498тМЛ. By K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 25) the verse is taught

Griffith

Mail thee with flesh against the flames of Agni; encompass thee about with fat and marrow; So will the bold One eager to attack thee with fierce glow fail to girdle and consume thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Taking the staff from the hand of the deceased man (gat─Б╠Бsu),
    together with hearing, splendor, strengthтАФthou just there, here may we,
    rich in heroes, conquer all scorners [and] evil plotters.
Notes
Griffith

From his dead hand I take the staff he carried, together with his lore and strength and splendour. There art thou, there; and here with good men round us may we o’ercome all enemies and foemen.

    prosperous good; come thou hitherward unto the world of the living.

nearly to 9 a, b, and our 59 c, d to 9 c, d. But RV. has for

b├бl─Бya; dh├бnur h├бst─Бd ─Бd├бd─Бn─Б mс╣Ыt├бsya ┼Ыriy─Б├н kс╣гatr─Б╠Бy─Б├║ тАЩjase b├бl─Бya;

Griffith

From his dead hand I take the bow he carried, together with his. power and strength and splendour. Having collected wealth and ample treasure, come hither to the- world of living beings.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА
